Welcome to [████ ███████!]<redacted| (after:1s)[(animate:?redacted, "flicker")] Today is your first day as the new manager for the Mergers and Acquisitions (M&A) division at private investment banking firm, Summit Capital Partners! You're now responsible for 40 employees below you, and all of their concerns and needs. You will be given choices on how you want to handle situations with your subordinates, but choose wisely! These situations will have consequences! Now, on to your first day! <div class='next'> (button:)[[NEXT]] </div> <div class='text'>You enter the building for the first time, and make your way up to the 8th floor–the floor that your department is on. You get off the elevator and see the office space for the first time: it's big and modern, with employees' cubicles filling up most of the space. You're greeted by a young woman with short black hair, sporting a bright smile and an eager look on her face: it's your new secretary, Jane! She introduces herself and tells you how happy she is to meet you, and that she's excited for you to be a part of the team. <div class='question'>How do you respond?</div> </div> (button:)[[Smile at width="300px" height="300px"> ] <div class='text'>While in the break room, you overhear some of your employees discussing their plan of unionizing. They say that the last manager was committing wage theft, and even though he was fired, they have yet to receive proper compensation for the thousands of dollars they are owed by this company. They talk about how that, along with their other frustrations with the company, is motivating them to try and unionize so that they can defend themselves from workers' rights violations. <div class='question'>How do you react to hearing this information?</div> </div> (button:)[[Support them]] (button:)[[Confront them]]Hm. You walk over to where the employees are standing, and tell them that you overheard their conversation. You tell them that unionizing isn't going to do anything, and that you and your superiors won't tolerste such insolence. If they want their compensation, they're just going to have to wait. You emphasize that any more acts of insubordination will be swiftly followed by write-ups and other disciplinary action. The employees are upset by this. They nod their heads and say nothing, but their eyes are filled with anger. You walk back to your office, and you can hear them murmuring to each other as you leave. Once you're back in your office, you open up your laptop and realize that you've received an [[email from your supervisor.]] <img In difficult situations like this, it's crucial to help ease the nerves of the employee as best as you can and create an environment that encourages an open dialogue between the both of you. You tell Alex to take a seat in one the chairs in front of your desk. You explain to him that your supervisors decided that the company needs to downsize, and instructed you to lay off some employees, starting with the newest hire. You let Alex know that if you had any say in this situation, you wouldn't be laying anyone off, but that your hands are unfortunately tied. You walk over to where the employees are standing, and tell them that you heard their conversation. You tell them that although you cannot legally join their union, you fully support their unionization. You add that even though unions aren't incredibly common in the financial sector, you think it would be a great for the workplace. Your employees are thrilled to hear this–it's a huge change in attitude from their previous manager. After talking with the employees for a few more minutes, you head back to your office to get more work done.
